電影消息

遜淸德菱郡主扮演「大地」一主角

— 萊

賽珍球布克夫人所作「大地」一書，早已遍傳世界，美國米高梅影片公司於三　前開始攝製，曾來華拍取喪機及其他中國民俗，後因導演喬治希爾Goger　Hill自殺逝世，擱淺甚久，數月前始恢復開拍，目下正在積極進行中。現又有一引人注目之消息，卽該片中荷花一角，由德菱郡主扮演之說，合同雖未簽訂，但郡主已在試演中則為事實。據聞德菱郡主曾在法國女伶沙拉班那（Sarah　Bnrnhardt）指導下學過戲劇，也曾隨美國鄧肯女士學過舞蹈，此為好萊塢影刊Cinema載之消息，確吾待攷，苟成事實，則此有關中華國體之女角，將由德菱演之矣。

按：沙拉班那為法國已故女名伶，聲　之大，殆有甚於梅蘭芳之在中國，沙女士演「茶花女」劇。力膾炙一時。至於鄧肯女士為美國古典派舞者之先進，為古典舞鼻祖Wagner之得意門人云。

歐美報章一致推薦的「小男兒」

明日起在國泰獻映

「小男兒」為奧爾珂德女士不朽名著。與其「小婦人」「好妻子」並誦於時。現已搬上銀幕。由好萊塢全班童星合演。成為年來美國片中罕見之珍品。片將於明日起。在國泰獻映。茲將歐美著名報章對該片之佳評譯錄一二。以餉　者。

「小男兒永遠打動你的心！」

「是美國羅羅蔓克電影最可寳貴的一部！」

「情愛，和平，動人，美麗……唯奧爾珂德筆底下才能濃郁地煊染這些。」

「萬衆一卷……在銀幕上一樣可以震驚全球。」

「使你會心的微笑……使你不期然的神往。」

「無疑為本年度鉅片之一。」

「是奧爾珂德作品中最可愛最光榮的一部。」

二廠

「生死同心」與「淸明時節」同時開拍

亞爾培路　明星第二廠成立以來將近一月，攝影場內部裝修完竣，「生死司心」與「淸明時節一（黎明輝主寅）卽司時開拍，日內「生死同心一正趕東陳波兒的戲，男主角袁牧之近來正從事研究劇中囚徒之化裝，照牧之過去之化裝經騐，在此戲中定有不少驚人供獻。

一廠

「夜會」「永遠的微笑」同時攝製

楓林橋總廠，一海棠紅」已全部攝竣，「小玲子」正在剪接，姚蘇鳳編劇之「夜會」（李萍倩導演）與劉吶鷗編劇之「永遠的微笑」（吳村導演）同時在工作緊張中，「夜會」係顧蘭君龔稼農等主演，龔稼農在此片中扮一瞎子，「、六遠的微笑」由胡蝶頒銜主演。

花花絮絮

本頭「春色」半月刋前後對面里共刋黎莉莉游泳照像九頓，「肉感美麗」，「只售大洋八分」。

據雨這年頭兒「謠言」都有些「費解」起來了。

「海棠紅」寫一個軍閥時代開始的故事，有一個那時代的督軍，他的「打過圖」和預定要「打圈」的女子照片竟洋洋大覜的集成了一巨册，當時的那些軍人官僚的交際中，談話的資料也大多取之於女人的隊伍中，一種腐爛毒害的官塲黑幕「海棠紅」是非常趣味而非常眞切的把它挑揭了出來。

藍蘋主演蔡楚生之新作「王老五」，條件大致商妥，合同日內可簽定。

「冷月狼烟錄」中需用之狼，將由各地（動物園借用。

藝華新片「廣陵潮」演員名單已排定，主演人為袁美雲，王引，開旋，朱飛等。

上海灘半月雜誌創刋號今日出版，內容以戲劇與電影為主，其他如眺舞，歌劇，播音，兒童等亦應有盡有，該刋主編劉亞偉極端歡迎「客觀底嚴　的商確」云。

周璇昨日在虹日游泳池演出，跳水姿勢極佳，大受注目。

1936.08.03

Yue Army Has Not Entered Guangxi; Guangxi Government Formation Difficult to Realize; Guangxi Decides to Increase Eight and Nine Armies; Various Wuzhou Agencies Move to Guiping; Rumor of Bai Chongxi's Family Arriving in Hong Kong; Foreign Nationals in Qinzhou and Lianzhou Ordered to Leave

(Hong Kong) As of the 2nd, the Yue Army has not entered Guangxi, making it difficult to form a Guangxi military government. The Central Government still wants to resolve the issue through political means. Yu Hanmou appointed the Guangxi veteran Huang Quan Mengzhi as a Four-Route Advisor. Foreign nationals in Qinzhou and Lianzhou have been ordered to leave. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Guangxi agents are causing disturbances in various parts of Guangdong. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) Various agencies in Wuzhou were ordered on the 2nd to relocate to Guiping. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Guangxi has decided to increase the Eighth and Ninth Armies. The commander of the Eighth Army is tentatively set as Li Pinxian, and the commander of the Ninth Army is Yang Zhenxian. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Bai Chongxi's wife, along with her children and more than 30 pieces of luggage, arrived in Hong Kong from Wuzhou on the Jiangning ship on the 2nd. She seems to intend to find a house and reside there for a long time. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Guiyang The Guizhou Provincial Party Headquarters wired the Central Government yesterday, stating that since the Second Plenary Session, the Central Government's policy for resolving the current situation has emphasized leniency, and it has not investigated the past actions of those who have deviated. However, Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi have other intentions and have delayed accepting their appointments. They also plan to form a bogus government to encroach on the Guangdong border. Although the Guangxi army in southern Guizhou has withdrawn, it has supplied a large number of funds and weapons to bandits like You Yu Jiu and Cao Tianquan, who are causing disturbances in various counties in southern Guizhou. Wherever the poisonous atmosphere reaches, cities become empty. Their stubborn adherence to their wrong ways and obvious rebellious actions have reached a point where there is no possibility of forgiveness. The Central Government should be requested to immediately transfer the matter to the National Government to issue a clear order for a punitive expedition, in order to maintain discipline and safeguard the nation's destiny. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Air Traffic Between Guangdong and Guangxi Severed

(Guangzhou) Starting on the 1st, the Tongli and Xi'an ships have stopped operating. Four Guangxi shallow-water warships are patrolling the areas of Wuzhou, Fengchuan, and Jiangkou, intercepting more than 100 civilian ships. The Liangguang Civil Aviation Company has ordered all ships under its jurisdiction to cease going to Wuzhou. Currently, news from Guangdong to Wuzhou is completely cut off. The Guangxi authorities have wired all Guangxi Bank branches to transport all foreign currency and cash held outside of accounts to Yongning and Liuzhou for centralization. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Suburbs of Nanning; People's Militia Disarmed and Dismissed; Li Pinxian's Attitude is Passive

(Hong Kong) Nanning, 2nd Dispatch: (1) Li Pinxian, with a certain country as his background, has betrayed the Central Government and severed ties with the Party and the nation. He visited Li Zongren on the evening of the 1st and earnestly advised him. It is said that Li is determined to go his own way. Li Pinxian's loyal advice was rejected, and he appears to be taking a passive stance and plans to leave Guangxi for elsewhere within the next few days. (2) The bogus autonomous government was originally scheduled to be established on the 1st, but it was ultimately changed to the 5th due to the opposition of the majority of the armed people's militia. 1,500 members of the people's militia stationed in the suburbs of Nanning were disarmed and dismissed on the afternoon of the 1st due to their opposition to Guangxi province colluding with a certain country to harm the country and the people. The deputy commander of the militia, Huang Guicun, was detained. The people's militia in various places are therefore opposing it even more fiercely. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Guangdong Army Reduced to Ten Divisions; Zhang Da and Miao Peinan to Go Abroad; Pacification Commissioner's Offices in Various Districts Abolished

(Hong Kong) The Guangdong army is being reorganized and reduced to ten divisions: 1st Division Commander Mo Xide, 2nd Ye Zhao, 3rd Zhang Ruigui, 4th Wu Jianxiong, 5th Li Hanhun, 6th Deng Longguang, 7th Huang Zhiwen, 8th Zeng Youren, 9th Tan Zhu, 10th Chen Hanguang. Zhang Da and Miao Peinan will go abroad for observation. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Pacification Commissioner's Offices in various districts of Guangdong are being abolished, with a deadline of the 8th. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Qian Zongze arrived in the province on the 2nd on a special train, with another train for office use. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Li Gang took over as the commander of the Military Police on the 2nd. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Yu Hanmou has redeployed Deng Longguang's division to defend Huizhou. The Guangdong Air Defense Association has been changed to the Air Defense Office, and Yu has appointed Gao Hanzhong as its director. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Xie Xizhen's regiment of the 1st Guangdong Army, which had been stationed in southern Jiangxi, arrived in the province on the 2nd. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Huang Musong Is Determined to Fly to Guangdong to Assume His New Post; Xu Chongqing Has Resigned and Is Being Persuaded; Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission Staff Hold Farewell Banquet

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Guangdong Provincial Chairman Huang Musong bid farewell to various parties on the 2nd. At noon, he attended a banquet hosted by Zhao Pilian, Deputy Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and Liang Hancao, Secretary-General of the Legislative Yuan. In the evening, he attended a banquet hosted by He Yingqin, the Minister of Military Affairs. After meeting with Lin Yunjie in Beijing, he will depart for Guangdong. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After the newly appointed Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, Huang Musong, returned to Beijing, he instructed the various departments of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission to expedite the handover matters so that the new Chairman Lin could come to Beijing to take over. If Lin does not arrive before Huang leaves Beijing, Zhao Pilian will act on behalf of Huang for all commission affairs, while Huang will designate several people to stay in Beijing to handle the handover matters. It is reported that the Guangdong Provincial Government will be reorganized and established before the 10th. Huang is scheduled to fly to Guangdong around the 6th to assume his post. Cen Xuelu and Liu Weizhi will travel with him. Xu Chongqing, the Director of Education of Guangdong Province, has expressed humility regarding his new position and is currently being persuaded by Huang. It has not yet been decided whether he will accompany Huang to Guangdong. Furthermore, all the staff of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission are reluctant to see Huang leave Beijing and specially hosted a banquet for Huang and Cen in the grand auditorium of the commission at noon on the 2nd. More than 100 staff members, including Zhao Pilian, attended. The atmosphere during the banquet was very cordial. After the banquet, photographs were taken. Huang also scheduled to attend the memorial service on the morning of the 3rd to give a farewell speech to all the staff. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Guangdong Finance Department Urges Rice Merchants to Pay Import Tax on Foreign Rice

(Hong Kong) The Finance Department issued a notice on the 2nd, urging rice merchants to pay import tax on foreign rice in order to protect domestic agriculture and maintain the integrity of customs duties. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Chen Youren Arrives in Nanning

(Guangzhou) Today, all the Chinese-language evening newspapers here published startling news, stating that the former Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, Chen Youren, has arrived in Nanning, the capital of Guangxi Province, and is holding discussions with the leaders of Guangxi Province. (2nd Reuters Dispatch)

Hurricane Hits Shantou and Xiamen; Maritime Traffic Severed

(Shantou) A hurricane arrived in Shantou on the 1st. There has been strong wind and rain since the afternoon, which has not stopped yet. Advertisements, signboards, awnings, debris, electric wires, trees, and other items are scattered all over the streets. Maritime traffic has been severed, and there has been significant damage to farmland. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Xiamen) The hurricane landed in Xiamen with great force at 2:00 AM on the 2nd, bringing strong winds and heavy rain from the northeast. The rain stopped in the afternoon, but the wind remained strong in the evening. The temperature dropped from 92 degrees to 82 degrees. Ocean liners and inland steamers, as well as the Zhangzhou-Quanzhou roadways, have all suspended operations. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Li Shilin Ordered to Visit Japanese Warships Docked in Xiamen

(Fuzhou) The Provincial Government has wired Li Shilin, instructing him to represent them in visiting the joint Japanese fleet docked in Xiamen and ordering the people of coastal counties not to misunderstand. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Feng Yuxiang Arrives at Kuling

(Anqing) Feng Yuxiang passed through Anhui at 6:00 AM on the 2nd aboard the Jianghua ship from Beijing. Miao Peicheng, Liu Zhenhua, and others boarded the ship to meet and talk with him. At 9:00 AM, he headed west to Xunyang to visit Chiang Kai-shek at Kuling. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Jiujiang) Kuling telephone report: Chen Shaokuan arrived at Kuling on the morning of the 2nd, and Feng Yuxiang arrived at Kuling at 8:00 PM on the 2nd. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Changsha) Yi Shuzhu wired He, arriving in Kuling on the 2nd, and met with Kong Xiangxi. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Telegrams Guangxi, Urging Li and Bai to Accept New Positions; Transfers to New Positions Have No Effect; Plans to Visit Guangdong in the Near Future; Eagerly Hopes to Have a Meeting and Conversation

(Jiujiang) Kuling telephone report: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek sent a telegram to Li and Bai on the 1st. The original text is as follows: Yongning, Li Delin, Bai Jiansheng, Admiration, I received your secret telegram on the 28th early on, and I have been waiting for your reply, but rumors on the street all say that you two will reject the new appointment and will not hesitate to resort to force, and there is even a rumor that a self-governing military government will be formed on August 1st. These kinds of rumors are spreading widely. I am saddened to hear them, but I do not believe that you two will take such action. Now, the rumor that a government will be formed on August 1st has not been realized, and I am even more confident that you two will be able to love the Party and the country and will never betray the Central Government, so as not to bring shame to the history of the revolution. I sent you a telegram, but I have not received a reply, and you have not indicated that you will take up the new position. My colleagues in the Central Government, and in private, receive telegrams that seem to indicate that you two still have some estrangement and misunderstandings with the Central Government, so I do not hesitate to express my earnest opinions to you two again. After repeatedly reviewing your recent telegrams to the comrades of the Central Government, I have summarized them to be about two points: (1) You believe that the Central Government's transfer of you two to new positions has another purpose. (2) You believe that the National Government's announcement of the new appointments is a violation of the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session, and even criticize it as being unlawful and untrustworthy. If you two observe in this way, this is truly a great misunderstanding. First, regarding the first point, I dare to tell you two frankly that the Central Government's new appointments are nothing more than, on the one hand, cherishing your revolutionary history and achievements, and relieving the difficulties of the environment in which you two are situated, so as to give full play to your talents to serve the Party and the country, and, on the other hand, thoroughly realizing the unification of the country, strengthening the unity of our Party, so that people can give full play to their talents and work together in a unified manner to develop strength to resist foreign aggression. If you want to talk about purpose, this is the only purpose. There is not a single word of falsehood in what I said in my telegram. If you two speculate from the perspective of malicious intent, you will be misled by a thousand miles. Moreover, before and after the Second Plenary Session, whenever I talked to my comrades in Guangxi about the Guangxi issue, I always thought that if this continued, you two would have irredeemable suffering, because since June 1st, the number of troops has more than doubled, military expenditures have increased sharply, the price of paper money has plummeted, commodity prices have been shockingly expensive, and society has been filled with sorrow. In addition, conscription of soldiers and grain has aroused resentment among the people. If they do not obey, they are imprisoned, and disturbances occur one after another, and the people are not at peace. Therefore, even if the issue of the military is not discussed, the social economy and the suffering of the people are like this, and I know that you two will not be able to improve the situation. At that time, the Central Government issued new orders for pacification, and at the same time, specially appointed you two as members of the National Defense Council, hoping that you two could come to Beijing to discuss in detail how to deal with the aftermath of the Guangxi situation, but you two hesitated and did not take up the positions, so I transferred Ji Kuan back to Guangxi and sent you two to the Central Government and Zhejiang Province, truly to put myself in your position, on the one hand, I could not but take into account the vitality of the people of Guangxi and the base on which you two have worked hard, and at the same time, I did not want you two to feel that it is not easy to untie the knot of the present national crisis. If things have reached this point, and the Central Government wants to entrust you two with the task of reorganizing the Guangxi situation and taking responsibility to the end, so as to restore the original state before June 1st, it would be forcing you two to do what is difficult. Therefore, this time, the transfer to new positions is really to preserve your good name for a long time, to leave the people of Guangxi with a good impression of you two, and the country can also rely on your talents. The Central Government's painstaking efforts and my sincerity in loving my friends are nothing more than this. If you two think about it calmly, it will not be difficult to dispel the misunderstanding on the first point. As for the second point, the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session and the orders of the government were all announced on July 13th, but on the 15th, you still held the so-called Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces. You not only did not show any observance of the Central Government's resolutions, but the Guangdong and Guangxi newspapers arbitrarily opposed the Central Government. I repeatedly instructed Ji Kuan, Bo Xuan, and Li Qing to send telegrams to persuade you, hoping that both public and private interests could be taken care of, so that the overall situation could be resolved satisfactorily, but you two did not give a clear reply. Later, although Bo Nan went to Hong Kong, I thought that you two would be able to accept the new position without any hesitation, but my expectations were in vain. Even after Wuo Qi returned to the province, and the order to develop had been issued for more than ten days, you two had not yet taken up the position. The government colleagues believed that you must have real difficulties if you two were hesitating, so they transferred you two to new positions as a place of transition. When the new order was announced, your telegrams expressing your intention to take up the positions arrived at the same time. Although there was a time difference, the Central Government's reliance on you two has not changed from the past. Since you two are willing to accept the previous mandate for pacification, there is no reason why you would not be willing to accept the new mandate. We have dedicated ourselves to the Party and the country, and we have been dispatched to various places. The scope is vast and there are many undertakings. Why must we be confined to a specific region to be able to show ourselves? Delin is serving in the Central Government and making greater contributions. Jiansheng has changed to preside over provincial administration. Zhejiang and Guangxi are both part of the country, so what choice is there to make? Therefore, if you two truly want to show your bright and open mind, to complete the unification and unity of the Party and the country, and to show the whole country the norms of supporting unification and obeying the Party and the country, then all orders should be gladly accepted without hesitation. As for the appointment of local officials, it is originally the authority of the government. The Plenary Session also did not restrict any changes. The powers and responsibilities of the Party and the government have always been stipulated in this way, and should not be regarded as violating the resolutions and criticized as being unlawful and untrustworthy. Since the new order was announced, it has been more than a week, and public opinion throughout the country has hoped that you two will maintain your good reputation and bring benefits to the country. However, you two have not yet shown any sign of accepting the Central Government's new mandate. Instead, I have heard that you are increasing defenses and building fortresses, and mobilizing troops, and there are even rumors that you two have the determination to attack Guangdong and invade Hunan. This is an extremely dangerous plan, and you two should carefully consider it. Whether the Central Government cherishes national power and hopes for peace has long been shown to China and foreign countries, and even the national public opinion will never allow the use of force and self-destruction internally. If you two send troops to neighboring provinces, please note that today's public opinion is definitely not what it used to be. If you enter or leave any province without the Central Government's order, no matter how strong your troops are, you will not be tolerated by the people and will only trap yourselves in a desperate situation. If we claim to be soldiers and citizens of China, then we will not only have no way to go if we do not follow the Central Government's orders, but we will also have no place to stand. Therefore, today we must recognize the trend of the times, respect the power of public opinion, and not rely solely on military force. All of the above, once analyzed, I know that you two will definitely agree with what I have said. However, there may be some who do not speak out, so I cannot but hope that you two will show a willingness to dispel public doubts. In short, the key to our success or failure today must be judged by conforming to reason and circumstances. Any measures that conform to reason and respond to circumstances will not fail. If they are contrary to the great righteousness of the revolution and contrary to the trend of the times, then going against reason and resisting the trend will not benefit either public or private interests. The main reason for this matter must be that we have been separated for too long. I have not been able to convey my sincere intentions to you two, my brothers who have shared life and death for many years, and I am deeply ashamed. I dare to express my heartfelt thoughts and state what I have seen, without concealment or embellishment, in detail to you two. I earnestly hope that you two will consider the interests of the country and the nation, value the sincerity of the Central Government and the expectations of the people, dispel all suspicions, and make a wise decision as soon as possible, accept the new mandate, and express your intention to take up the position, so as to show your true sincerity of being selfless and devoted to the public, and to comfort the eager expectations of the whole country. In the shortest period of time, I also plan to visit Guangdong and sincerely hope to have a meeting and conversation with you two to discuss in detail the full range of issues so that unification can be realized, peace can be achieved, and the country and the local area can benefit, and everything can be discussed thoroughly to formulate a long-term plan for the country, which will also consolidate the foundation of the revolution. If you agree with my humble words, please reply by telegram to show your intent, and I will set off to Guangdong immediately to discuss everything in person. We have shared hardships for many years, and I am confident that we will be able to come together to show our sincerity and comfort the spirit of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen in heaven. Words cannot express all my thoughts, and I only hope that you will carefully consider them. Chiang Kai-shek, East (1st), Printed. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Shi Jingting Meets Han and Passes Through Jinan to Tianjin to Go to Beiping

(Tianjin) Shi Jingting came to Tianjin from Jinan on the morning of the 2nd after meeting with Han. He visited Zhang Zizhong and took the evening train to Beiping to meet with Song. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Songshi's Remarks: There is currently no diplomacy to speak of in North China. The negotiations in eastern Hebei do not count as diplomacy. Developing the economy of North China requires the military to be the center. Using Japanese technicians for the Cangshi Road can also help with funding. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Ji Liang, a member of the Construction Committee, will go to Jinan at 8:00 PM tonight to convey a message on behalf of Song to Han. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Tianjin Municipal Government Implements Staff Reduction and Salary Cuts

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Municipal Government is implementing austerity measures. On the 2nd, it laid off seven staff members and more than ten clerks from the first, second, and third sections. The salaries of senior officials have been reduced. The city's expenditures for the 25th year of the Republic will not exceed six million. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Song Zheyuan Inspects Troops Stationed in Nanyuan

(Beiping) This morning, Song Zheyuan, accompanied by Zou Decheng and Feng Zhi'an, went to Nanyuan to inspect the troops of the 37th Division and visited the headquarters of the 29th Army. He returned to the city in the afternoon. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan originally planned to go to Baoding on the 11th, but it was temporarily postponed due to some matters. On the morning of the 2nd, he went to Nanyuan with Feng Zhi'an and others to inspect the garrison troops and gave a speech to the soldiers, instructing them to pay attention to summer hygiene. He returned to the city at noon. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) The newly appointed advisor to the Hebei Political Council, Nishida Koichi, is scheduled to come to Beiping from Tianjin tomorrow afternoon, stay for one day to arrange his residence, and then go to Tianjin to pick up his family. He will then meet with Song to ask for instructions on everything. The Japanese Consul General in Tianjin, Tajiri, is scheduled to come to Beiping tomorrow to visit Song. Song will host a banquet at the Diplomatic Building that evening for a joyful gathering. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Yin Rugeng Arrives in Tianjin to See off Yongjian and Others; Visits Tadashi and Tajiri for Heartfelt Talks

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng came to Tianjin on the evening of the 1st with Liu Zongji and Wang Xiacai to send off Yongjian, Ishii, Hayashi, Otake, and others back to their country. At 9:00 AM on the 2nd, he visited Tadashi at the Zhangyuan official residence, and at 11:00 AM, he visited Tajiri at the Consul General's residence for heartfelt talks. In the afternoon, he hosted a banquet at Dongxinglou to see off Yongjian and others. He plans to return to Tongzhou on the 4th. Six tank cars of the Japanese military tank unit in Tianjin will be transported to Nanda Temple on the morning of the 3rd to participate in a large-scale exercise by the garrison troops in Yuqin. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Major General Hashimoto Gun, the newly appointed Chief of Staff of the Japanese garrison in North China, is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin on the Changcheng Maru on the 15th to take office. Yongjian will leave Tianjin on the 18th to return to his country. Staff Officer Hayashi Yoshishu will return to his country on the 5th, and Ishii will return to his country on the 10th and be transferred to a new post. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Tianjin Rogues Plan to Form Armed Smuggling Groups; Smuggled Goods Piling Up, Unable to Be Cleared; No Shipment From Tianjin to South Via Jinpu Railway for Half a Month

(Tianjin) No smuggled goods have been shipped south from Tianjin via the Jinpu Railway for half a month. Since the 1st, the Tianjin suburbs of Wuhe have been patrolled by the Water Police Bureau, the Security Command, military police, and customs personnel to crack down on smuggling. Customs has ordered the tax bureau to strictly investigate customs officials who are found to be shielding smuggling activities. Customs officials suspected of serious involvement have been transferred to other ports. Seeing that smuggled goods are piling up in Tianjin and prices have plummeted, the rogues are planning to form armed smuggling groups to try to transport goods to southern Hebei and northern Jiangsu. They are currently organizing a suicide squad. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Jinpu Railway has reiterated the order that railway protection police must not shield or leak smuggled goods or goods on which taxes have not been paid. Those found to be in violation will be severely punished. Li Tonghua, Deputy Director of the Inspection Department of the Ministry of Finance, is scheduled to come to Tianjin on the 3rd to meet with Xu Lixia, the Tianjin Customs Commissioner, to discuss strategies for intercepting smuggled goods from eastern Hebei being transported to Tianjin. The smuggling rogue trade association in a certain concession in Tianjin is showing signs of disintegration. The member smuggling firms are automatically lowering prices, undermining each other, and seeking to clear smuggled goods. Several smuggling companies have collapsed last week. The smuggling situation in a certain concession is no longer as rampant as it was two months ago. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Li Tonghua, Deputy Director of the Anti-Smuggling Office, arrived in Jinan from Beijing on the Pinghu train at around 10:00 AM on the morning of the 2nd to inspect the road transportation smuggling matters and the road transportation anti-smuggling work. After strict investigation and crackdown on smuggled goods, road transportation has now disappeared. Ansiir is currently in Jiaodong. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Jinan Executes Sixty-One Bandits

(Jinan) Today, sixty-one notorious bandits, including Xu Xiaogan, were brought to Jinan and all were executed by firing squad. Soldiers and officers who suppressed the bandits were awarded 20,000 yuan. (2nd Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Xu Xiaogan, a famous bandit leader, led more than sixty fierce bandits and occupied the area on the border between Jiangsu and Shandong. Han Fuju sent his adjutant Zhang Buyun to suppress them. After capturing Xu Xiaogan and 61 others alive, including one female bandit, Han sent an armored car to escort them to Jinan on the 1st day and night. On the morning of the 2nd, at 8:00 AM, Han sent someone to interrogate them at the Jiaoji Station, and then they were bound and taken to the north of Chenfeng Bridge for execution by firing squad. The female bandit was sent to a relief home to learn a craft. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

National Government Officially Appoints Long Yun as Pacification Commissioner of Yunnan and Guizhou; Xue Yue as Deputy Pacification Commissioner; Gu Zhutong as Chairman of Guizhou Province

(Nanjing) The National Government issued the following official decree on the 2nd: The Headquarters of the Yunnan-Guizhou Bandit Suppression Commander-in-Chief shall be abolished immediately. This order.

Specially appoint Long Yun as the Pacification Commissioner of Yunnan and Guizhou, and Xue Yue as the Deputy Commissioner. This order.

Wu Zhongxin, a member of the Guizhou Government and Chairman, has requested to resign. Wu Zhongxin is hereby permitted to be relieved of all his concurrent positions. This order.

Appoint Gu Zhutong as a member of the Guizhou Provincial Government. This order.

Appoint Gu Zhutong concurrently as the Chairman of the Guizhou Provincial Government. This order. (2nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Current Grain Situation in Beijing

(Nanjing) According to the City Grain Association, this year's wheat harvest is extremely abundant, and wheat ships and merchants coming to Beijing to purchase wheat are very enthusiastic. Now the wheat season in the market has ended. This month, the average number of wheat ships per day is one hundred and dozens. Because of the poor sales of local wheat, only a dozen or so flour mills remain in Beijing. The Datong Flour Company has stockpiled 200,000 Zu (a unit of measurement), and grain stores and mills have purchased less than 100,000 Dan (another unit of measurement). Gaorongchang, Chentongji, Yutong, and other grain stores purchased 600,000 Dan on behalf of the Shanghai Fuxing Flour Company. Initially, the price was 4 yuan and 12 jiao per Dan, but now it has risen to 5 yuan and 12 jiao. New grains have entered the market in various places, and many rice ships have arrived in recent days. There are more than 40 rice ships outside the Zhonghua Gate every day, carrying up to 2,000 Shi (another unit of measurement) of rice. There are even more at Xiaguan, so the price of rice has fallen. The current market price for Ju rice is 6 yuan and 6 or 7 jiao per Dan, Huangshu rice is about 9 yuan, and Heishu rice is 10 yuan, 1 or 2 jiao, and the price is likely to continue to fall. New rice from the suburbs of Beijing will be available on the market in the middle of the month, and new rice from Jiangbei and Anhui province will arrive in Beijing in large quantities around the 20th. Shanghai rice merchants have recently entrusted rice stores in Beijing to purchase large quantities of rice, but because the rice stores that stockpiled rice last year have suffered great losses, other buyers can maintain their operations. Zhonghua Gate has always been a rice market, but since the Beijing-Wuhu Railway opened, business has declined sharply, because the rice stores in the city who used to purchase from the grain mills are now going directly to Anhui to purchase, which can save brokerage fees and the expenses of measuring grains. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Reality of Rural Revival

— Liu

For years, all Chinese people have regarded relieving farmers as a crucial goal. There are various ways to provide relief, but the ultimate aim is to revitalize the countryside. What is the effectiveness of the implemented plans? It is difficult to predict. However, based on what has been seen and heard, there are things that one cannot help but speak about. Unified marketing is intended to facilitate the sale of agricultural products and to eliminate exploitation by middlemen. The intention is good. However, to prevent investment losses, purchase prices are deliberately suppressed, so the farmers' income may actually be less than before. This is not the original intention of unified marketing. Unified marketing should first promote quality and balance supply and demand so that farmers can avoid unwarranted losses and the countryside can have hope for revitalization. Now, it is often the opposite. Purchasing raw materials at low prices and selling finished products at high prices merely creates opportunities for merchants. As for establishing warehouses to store agricultural products, let's not discuss whether the methods can be better than pawnshops accepting agricultural products as collateral. If the valuation is slightly higher (close to the market price), then losses are expected when the market price declines. If it is lower, how can it be justified to the farmers as not exploiting them? If merchants' goods are accepted to facilitate turnover, it is feared that it will strengthen the merchants and the profits will go to them. When urban financial power suddenly enters the countryside, the environment changes drastically, and the appearance is no longer the same. Without this foundation, wanting to achieve this is like forcibly transplanting foreign rules to China. It is unlikely that it will not be full of setbacks.

Rural investment is not the business of commercial banks. In recent years, they have sometimes hesitated to provide loans for industrial, commercial, and real estate purposes. With no outlet for funds, they are moving towards the interior. This way, they can achieve their profit-making goals and gain a reputation for revitalizing the countryside. Moreover, since it is legally required to invest one-fourth of savings deposits in rural areas, there are no worries about acting in accordance with the law. Even those who do not like operating in this way have to do some token investment to comply with the law. Many people think that investing in rural areas is very safe, but they do not understand that rural lending is a specialized business that ordinary commercial banks cannot handle. Even if it is used as a reserve for savings deposits, there is room for study on whether it is mutually beneficial. In recent years, bank closures have been frequently heard, but how their savings deposits are handled is rarely seen in the newspapers. In normal times, they call for unlimited liability, but the results of their operations are still like this. The rest can be imagined.

This year, farmers seem to have breathed a sigh of relief. This is due to the rise in the price of soybeans and wheat, and its cause is the same as the rise in tung oil last year, coming from abroad. Soybean prices are manipulated by Dalian. In the past year, the price of soybean cake has increased several times. Wheat has been affected by speculation in the futures market and purchases by Japanese merchants, and prices have also increased significantly. Although it is not what flour mills want, farmers are happy. However, price fluctuations are at the mercy of others, and we do not have control over whether prices are high or low. Even if there are gains temporarily, the danger is worrying, because our country, even with soybeans and wheat, is not self-sufficient.

From all aspects, although the call for relief is high, the suffering of farmers has not been eliminated. This is probably due to the inconsistency between theory and practice. Farmers are most conservative, especially in our country. Most of them are uneducated, so new facilities inevitably seem incompatible. Therefore, without in-depth study based on reality, it is not only futile but also causes farmers to feel annoyed and inconvenienced, which is contrary to the original purpose of relief. If we think from the perspective of farmers' actual lives, guide them according to circumstances, and improve things, then there may be hope for successful rural revitalization.

The Jingqu Railway Officially Starts Construction

(Nanjing) The Jingqu Railway, starting from Xuancheng in Anhui Province and heading south through Quzhou in Zhejiang Province, is now under construction in separate sections. Construction officially began last week and is expected to be completed in three years. As for the Jiliao Railway, it is necessary to cross the Yellow River. If a new railway bridge is built, it will cost a lot. To save expenses, it has been decided to borrow the Jinpu Yellow River Bridge. The joint route starts from Jinan and passes through Changqing, Renping, and other counties in Shandong Province to Liaocheng. The budget is 6 million yuan. The fundraising for the project is jointly undertaken by the Shandong Provincial Government and the Ministry of Railways. Shandong Province has already recruited merchant shares, and the Ministry of Railways is also raising funds. The council is located in Jinan. Surveying will be completed within the year, and construction will be completed in three years. (2nd Day Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Communications Pays Attention to the Suffering of Boatmen

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau requested that a new penalty rule be formulated for overdue inspections of sailboats, and that the navigation authorities handle it themselves. The Ministry of Communications replied that sailboats often do not have a fixed freight rate, and overdue inspections are inevitable. To be considerate, the case should be handled according to the severity of the situation, and they should be sent to the court for punishment or warned separately. The navigation authorities should also provide explanations of laws and regulations at any time to make them understand, so that boatmen can reduce suffering. The section on self-punishment is not approved. (2nd Day Special Dispatch)

France Asks Britain and Italy to Maintain Neutrality Towards Spain, Otherwise It Will Also Supply Arms to the Country; German Cruiser Sails into Rebel Port

(Paris) Official sources recently stated that the French government will send telegrams to the British and Italian governments this afternoon, asking them to strictly maintain neutrality towards the Spanish situation and to implement it immediately. Once replies are received from the British and Italian governments, the same request will be made to countries related to the western Mediterranean. The government has now clearly announced that although France previously unilaterally decided to prohibit the transport of arms to Spain, the Spanish rebels are now being supplied with arms by foreign countries, so France believes that it is no longer bound by this unilateral decision. It is hoped that the countries concerned will have satisfactory answers on the issue of maintaining neutrality, so that the current difficulties can be quickly eased, and the international disputes that are already pressing can be avoided. Official sources also said that the French government's aspirations are nothing more than two points: (1) Foreign interference in the Spanish civil strife will have international implications, and this danger should be avoided; (2) The current Spanish government is the legitimate government, which has been officially recognized by various countries. The government is now engaged in suppressing the rebellion in order to restore domestic peace and order, and France should maintain friendly relations with this legitimate government. (1st Day Havas Dispatch)

(London) The French Embassy delivered a note to the Foreign Office this morning, arguing that the countries along the Mediterranean should immediately establish an agreement to strictly maintain neutrality toward the Spanish civil strife. Because the Foreign Office will not be open for business until Tuesday morning, it is difficult to ascertain the British official attitude at this time. However, people at the French Embassy believe that this note has been sent by the Foreign Office's duty personnel to Prime Minister Baldwin and Foreign Secretary Eden, both of whom expressed sympathy for it. Some people in diplomatic circles believe that the British government will definitely maintain its original position, that is, the supply of arms to Spain, whether from official or private sources, is prohibited, but ordinary trade between Britain and Spain should not be interfered with. (2nd Day Havas News Agency Dispatch)

Gibraltar A cruiser flying the German flag arrived at Algeciras in Cadiz Bay, Gibraltar, this afternoon. The name of the ship is currently unknown. Algeciras is now in the hands of the rebels. (2nd Day Reuters Dispatch)

France Releases Detained British Aircraft

Four Fokker aircraft belonging to the British Airways Company in Bordeaux, France, originally intended to fly to the capital of Portugal. When they passed through this port, they were detained by the authorities of the Gironde Province for several days. After negotiations by the British government, the French government has allowed them to fly back to Britain. The aircraft flew from here to London today, ending a dispute. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Italy Aiding Spanish Rebels, Britain Feels Uneasy; Italy Denies Coveting Morocco

(London) Regarding the matter of several Italian Savoia aircraft flying to Spanish Morocco, well-informed sources here recently stated that the aircraft belong to the country's official air force. It is also rumored that Spanish rebel leader General Franco has reached an agreement with the Italian government, promising certain political interests in exchange for Italian assistance to the rebels. It is most likely that the political interests will be given to Italy in the Balearic Islands. People on the right wing here, who previously sympathized with the Spanish rebels, immediately thought that if General Franco were to win, the result would inevitably have an adverse impact on Britain, so their attitude has changed. In addition, the Italian government is currently investigating the aircraft incident. Once the investigation has results, it will notify France, and the French government will forward it to Britain. Political figures here expect that the investigation results will not be satisfactory. As for France's intention to convene a conference of countries related to the Mediterranean, including Britain, France, and Italy, political figures still believe that it is better to conduct talks through diplomatic channels than to convene a full meeting. If a full meeting is held, it cannot be successful unless Russia and Germany participate together. However, the two countries are in opposition to each other, so it is difficult to ensure the conference's success. In addition, France has also suggested convening a conference of countries that guarantee the neutral status of the port of Tangier. This is also opposed by political figures, because Spanish warships are allowed to refuel in British Gibraltar, but it is unfair to prohibit them in Tangier. In short, Britain and France are currently closely linked on this issue. The future trend will be determined by the results of Italy's investigation of the aircraft incident. Political figures also pointed out that the British and French governments have agreed to prohibit all arms from being transported to Spain, while ordinary commercial goods can be freely exported without restrictions. This can be seen from the fact that the four Fokker aircraft belonging to British Airways Company have been released by the authorities of the port of Bordeaux, France, and returned to Britain. (1st Day Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) It is widely rumored here that the Italian Fascist Party has reached an agreement with the Spanish right-wing rebels. If the Fascist Party succeeds in this revolution, Spain will cede a port in the Balearic Islands to Italy. Since the Italian bomber crashed on the Moroccan border on July 30, the panic of international disputes has been increasing. (1st Day National Dispatch)

(Rome) A foreign newspaper published a statement by Spanish Foreign Minister Basilio, saying that Italy has coveted Spanish Morocco. The Italian newspaper here recently published an article refuting this statement, saying, "No one in our country has any intention of interfering in Spanish Morocco. It was like this in the past, and it is still the same now. The Spanish Foreign Minister's slanderous remarks give our country reason to refute them." In addition, rumors that Spanish rebel leader General Franco is willing to cede Ceuta to Italy as a reward for Italian assistance to the rebels have also been denied by the newspaper. (1st Day Havas Dispatch)

Tetouan, Spanish Morocco Spanish rebel Chief of Staff General Armada recently told our reporter that the Italian aircraft that landed in French territory did fly to Spanish Morocco, but their purpose was to transport Italian expatriates back to their country. Our reporter questioned why so many machine guns were found in these aircraft. General Armada replied, "I have said everything I want to say, and I do not want to elaborate." Our reporter then asked when the war would end. General Armada replied, "The reason why we have not won a great victory immediately is due to Soviet interference and the failure of a part of the navy to respond. But our army will launch a major offensive soon and will win a complete victory." Our reporter saw seven aircraft parked at the airport here, two of which were German Junkers, and one was Italian Savoia. It is not known whether there are other aircraft parked in the hangar. Our reporter then went to Ceuta and encountered ten trucks full of foreign troops heading to Ceuta. It can be seen that General Franco is indeed planning to transport foreign troops to mainland Spain by sea or by air. Although Ceuta has been bombed by government warships and aircraft in recent days, it has not suffered major damage. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Madrid The Spanish left-wing government is furious today because foreign aircraft are helping the rebels resist the government. The authorities here warned other countries that neighboring countries that help the rebels will be considered an act of war or will trigger a European war. The left-wing newspaper "Claridad" also said today that the rebels may hope that Fascist countries will provide assistance, and specifically named Portugal, Italy, and other countries. At the same time, the government ordered all administrative staff of universities and middle schools to be dismissed and replaced by new people appointed by the Ministry of Education within two weeks. The Ministry of the Interior ordered soldiers not to freely supplement or search private residences. Travelers returning here from Guadarrama reported today that the battle there was fierce and similar to the situation during the European war. (1st Day National Dispatch)

Madrid Foreign Minister Basilio recently told the press that after Ambassador to Italy Di Castelci and Ambassador to Germany Godinho successively resigned, the government ordered Ambassador to Switzerland Arciniega to be promoted to Ambassador to Italy, and Minister to Norway Miskovic to be transferred to Chargé d'Affaires to Germany. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Riga, Latvia Spanish Minister Curtis recently resigned to the Madrid government because he sympathized with the rebels in that country. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

The Spanish War is in a Stalemate on All Fronts; Government Forces Make Slight Progress; Rebels Eagerly Await Reinforcements

Madrid The government claimed victory today on both the northern and southern fronts. Although the rebels have controlled some provinces, they have still not broken through the gates of Madrid. The rebels have also failed to defend Albacete to cut off Madrid's food supply, which is a mistake. (1st Day National Dispatch)

Madrid Since the outbreak of the rebellion, the northern city of San Sebastian has experienced fierce fighting, and foreign expatriates have fled. Our reporter was able to enter the city with great difficulty and sent a telegram saying that although the city is still in a state of war, streetcars are running as usual, but few shops have reopened. Governor Adora told our reporter that the rebels are still entrenched in Pamplona in Navarre Province. They previously attempted to seize Irun, Oyarzun, and Renteria, but were repelled by our troops. They then attempted to attack government troops down the Oria River, but were also unsuccessful. As for the government troops' battle plan, they are currently planning to form two columns to advance towards Pamplona and Logroño in order to wipe them out in one fell swoop. In addition, the situation in Valencia Province in the southeast is stable, as is Catalonia Province. The government troops in that province, starting from Barcelona, are now approaching the rebel base of Zaragoza. In short, the government troops will surely win, it is only a matter of time." (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Barcelona Huesca is still occupied by the rebels. Government troops are advancing towards the city, and the outposts are only four kilometers from the city. An attack will be ordered today or at the latest tomorrow. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Madrid Two trains loaded with military supplies from Alcázar to Valladolid were bombed by several government aircraft. The boilers of the two locomotives were hit and exploded, and all the vehicles derailed. All the military supplies on board exploded. The aircraft then flew back to Valladolid and bombed the rebels, setting several fires in the city. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Gibraltar Regarding the Spanish war news, there were no major developments between the government forces and the rebels last night. Both sides seem to want to avoid a decisive battle at present and are only engaged in strategic arrangements in order to wait for the opportunity to move. The rebels obviously want to link up the northern and southern fronts and attack the capital Madrid from both sides, while the government forces are sharpening their swords and preparing to meet them head-on. This is the main point. The rebel radio station in Seville broadcast a very simple message last night, only saying that there was a small contact between the two sides in the Somosierra and Guadarrama areas north of the capital, and the situation did not change. It also said that the security team in Castellón Province in the east had indeed rebelled. On the other hand, the Madrid government issued a message saying that the government forces had won a slight victory. It also said that although the security team in a village 100 kilometers from Avila had rebelled a few days ago, it surrendered to the government yesterday. The security team in the village of Ispor in Granada Province also surrendered to the government forces. According to non-official sources, the village of Sastaigo near Zaragoza has recently been recaptured by the government forces. Also, the government troops led by General Asensio are now only eight kilometers away from Granada Province. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Swedish Merchant Ship Found Carrying Arms

(Paris) A Swedish merchant ship recently anchored in the port of Sète in the Hérault Province and was scheduled to sail to the Canary Islands in Spain (one of the rebel bases in the Atlantic) on the 3rd of this month. Officials discovered that the ship was carrying 15 tons of explosives and 50 kilograms of bomb detonators. The local Spanish consul has asked the Madrid government for instructions on this matter. (1st Day Havas Dispatch)

Many headless bodies have been found along the coast of Malaga. Anglo-Egyptian Treaty, Sudanese Articles Signed, Stipulating Joint Administration System

Cairo Regarding the various military articles of the new treaty negotiated between Britain and Egypt, an agreement has recently been reached. Subsequently, negotiations on the Sudanese issue continued, and an agreement has also been reached, and a preliminary signing was held yesterday, stipulating that the Sudanese region should restore the Anglo-Egyptian joint administration system before 1914. The Sudanese region, south of mainland Egypt, along the upper reaches of the Nile, was originally part of Egypt. After 1899, it was changed to Anglo-Egyptian joint administration. In 1924, Britain recognized Egypt as an independent country, and at the same time regarded Sudan as a British colony. (2nd Day Havas Dispatch)

Cairo The Sudanese articles of the Anglo-Egyptian Treaty were signed last night by British Commissioner in Egypt Sir Lampson and Egyptian Prime Minister Nahas here. The military articles of the Anglo-Egyptian Treaty were agreed upon on July 23, and now the Sudanese articles have also been compromised. Thus, the two major obstacles to the Anglo-Egyptian Treaty have been eliminated. Last night, the Egyptian government issued a communiqué stating that the Sudanese articles had been signed at the Anniatia Palace, and that other articles will now be negotiated. (1st Day Reuters Dispatch)

Tibetan Authorities Hire British Official

Shimla The Tibetan authorities have hired Mr. Gold, the British political officer in Bhutan, to Lhasa. It is said that Mr. Gold will set off in the next few days to take over the work of the late Mr. Williamson. Mr. Williamson was hired by the Tibetan authorities to mediate between the Tibetan authorities and the Panchen Lama. He recently died of chronic uremia in Lhasa. (2nd Day Reuters Dispatch)

Japanese Army Minister Will Urge Cabinet to Implement Innovative Administration, Believing it is the Remaining Mission After the Military Purge

(Tokyo) Expanding armaments, thoroughly purging the military, and reforming the administration are the three major missions declared by Army Minister Terauchi, who took office after the February 26th Incident. This regular military reshuffle was also carried out from the perspective of thoroughly purging the military, making considerable sacrifices. Regarding the declaration at the time of taking office, there is no regret in the implementation. However, the Army Minister's plan to thoroughly purge the military was originally intended to be realized simultaneously with expanding armaments and reforming the administration. Only by integrating the whole can its significance be expressed. Therefore, regarding the realization of reforming the administration, it is considered that it is extremely difficult to implement only by the army. It should be a prerequisite that the entire cabinet has the determination to implement it. However, regarding the expansion of armaments, the army has established a new twelve-year national defense enrichment plan, and the 3 billion yuan required for the first six years has been roughly grasped. The army has notified the government of this situation. In view of the current international situation, the army believes that this level of military expansion is a minimum estimate and should be realized. Therefore, the army, taking the February 26th Incident as an opportunity, has now begun to implement the purge and expansion of the military, and has established its own policy. The only remaining part is the part recognized by the government or the financial authorities, which will be a matter for the future. The Army Minister is gradually realizing the purge and expansion of the military, and the only remaining issue is the reform of the administration, which is his mission. However, the army's hope for this matter is the reform of administrative institutions, the stability of national life, and the establishment of a national policy towards Manchuria. The army has already notified the cabinet of the above-mentioned matters in official documents. However, regarding the comprehensive control and planning of national policy, the government has not yet decided on its attitude. Therefore, Army Minister Terauchi's hope for the Hirota cabinet to reform the administration is extremely strong. He will earnestly urge the government to make a decision and implement it. (2nd Day Allied Dispatch)

Japanese Economy: Plans to Develop in the South Seas, Stating No Ambition to Expand Territory

(Tokyo) Japanese diplomatic work is based on maintaining and developing the people's livelihood, centered on the inseparable relationship between Japan and Manchuria, and focusing on adjusting diplomatic relations with China and Russia. However, South Seas policy is also an important part of diplomatic work. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in order to adjust the relationship between various policies and achieve unified diplomacy, will establish a South Seas Section within the Eurasian Bureau in mid-September. Japan's South Seas policy has no territorial ambitions, and is only based on economic development. It goes without saying that it will avoid unnecessary oppression of the South Seas islands and handle all issues with a peaceful attitude. The implementation of the South Seas policy must consider the positions of Britain and the Netherlands, which have Australia and the Dutch East Indies as their background, and its countermeasures are extremely cautious and calm. Recently, proponents of Japan's southward advance policy have been loudly advocating the South Seas policy, causing Australia and the Dutch East Indies to feel threatened, making it difficult for the Japanese government to take a stand in this regard. In view of this fact, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided on a policy to implement a unified South Seas policy. (2nd day Allied News)

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Uchisawa, the Consul-General in Manila, the Philippine Assembly is currently deliberating on a number of bills that have a significant impact on Japanese companies, goods, and exports to the Philippines. Although most of them were proposed by government representatives, they seem likely to pass the Assembly and become law. Therefore, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is very concerned that the implementation of these laws will have a significant impact on the 30,000 Japanese residents in the Philippines and the annual exports to the Philippines, which amount to 50 million yuan. It has ordered Consul-General Uchisawa to actively lobby to prevent their passage through the Assembly. If these laws are enacted, their implementation requires the approval of the President of the United States, so Japan still has room to negotiate with the US government. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs also believes that since Japan's exports to the Philippines exceed imports by 30 million yuan annually, it will not rely solely on protests to deal with the Philippines. It plans to use economic cooperation to ease Philippine sentiments. (2nd day Allied News)

Soviet-Outer Mongolian Relations: Russian Ambassador's Speech at Oxford

(London) Soviet Ambassador Maisky recently delivered a speech at the Oxford Summer School, referring to the relationship between the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia. He stated, "The Soviet Union has no imperialistic intentions towards Outer Mongolia. What it is promoting is a socialist policy. Therefore, Outer Mongolia also views the Soviet Union with goodwill, and a genuine friendship between the two countries has emerged spontaneously." Maisky then described the Soviet Union's assistance to the Outer Mongolian Revolutionary Party in transforming the country, saying that the Soviet Union's actions were devoid of any profit-seeking motives. "There used to be commercial relations between the two countries, and there still are, but these are normal trade relations based on the principle of equality. An examination of the profit and loss figures of Russian-Mongolian trade will reveal that the Soviet Union actually suffers more losses than gains." In short, Russia and Mongolia have no mutual exploitation, and their relationship is completely new, created only after the establishment of socialist countries. Therefore, Mongolia's friendly relations with the Soviet Union are a matter of course. Even now, when facing external threats, it turns to the Soviet Union for help, as it did in 1921, there is nothing surprising about it. Russia and Mongolia fought together fifteen years ago, resulting in a sincere friendship. In March of this year, they signed a mutual assistance pact, which is nothing more than a reaffirmation of this friendship, with no other intention." Finally, Maisky mentioned the Anglo-Russian naval agreement, saying that it could be signed soon. (2nd day Havas News)

Military Purge Changes and Coups (1)

— Jia He

One of the special products of Japanese politics after "May 15th" is the "military purge." Minister of the Army Hayashi caused a huge disaster for the sake of the military purge. Now Minister of the Army Terauchi is also working hard on this, which makes every Japanese person, every person who cares about Japanese politics, inevitably ask in unison: Is a "military purge" possible? Who is the target of the "military purge"? Will it cause waves similar to the "February 26th" incident?

Although "changes" are periodic, they have become an indicator of Japanese political trends since Minister of the Army Hayashi took office and demonstrated his personnel skills. Before each "change," there are many news reports speculating about it. After it is announced, tens of thousands of people discuss and criticize it. Minister of the Army Terauchi has made many decisive personnel changes since taking office. It is said that "the August 1st change is the key to past changes. It will point out to us the extent to which the "military purge" work has been achieved and what the political significance indicated in the list of "changes" is. If the military is considered the core of exploring Japanese politics, then understanding the lineup of the military after the "changes" and the political trends presented by that lineup is indeed a necessary and essential common sense for the people of the Republic of China at this stage.

The mission of the Hirota Cabinet, from the day it received the mandate, was "military purge" and "international coordination." When the cabinet changed its chief of staff, it replaced "international coordination" with "renewal of all government affairs." "Military purge" has been on the main agenda of policy implementation since the establishment of the Saito Cabinet, but because of Araki Sadao's sharp edge, he did not dare to touch it. The Okada Cabinet, which changed the soup but not the medicine, touched it and provoked a coup that "aggravated the Emperor's concerns." Now the Hirota Cabinet dares to take on this task, which seems incomprehensible. "Renewal of all government affairs" is what Hirota dared to say and write, borrowing the courage of the military. He dares to give scathing criticism to past cabinets, at least the Saito and Okada cabinets, which seems incomprehensible. However, if we connect these two incomprehensible things, we will understand at a glance. "Military purge" and "renewal of all government affairs" are related. The day the "military purge" is completed (?), should be the time for the Hirota Cabinet's "renewal of all government affairs." If "military purge" cannot renew all government affairs, there will inevitably be a force like Mount Tai pressing on Hirota's back, which is the "coup." Here, we should quickly state to our readers: In "good neighborly relations" with the same race and culture, "coup" does not necessarily require the actions of Shiro Nonaka-style Showa Bushido. Even the change of cabinet can use this startling term. Therefore, from "military purge" to "changes," and from "changes" to "coup," I am afraid that it has already been predetermined in the fate of the Hirota Cabinet, hasn't it?

Since these three questions have become the core of exploring Japanese politics at this stage, should we discuss them in detail from all aspects? That is necessary, but there is no such plan in this article, because almost all other issues related to it have been discussed in the previously published "Where is the Hirota Cabinet Going?". Now, exploring from the point of view of the rise and fall of military factions, it may be possible to say what others have not said, and it may be more suitable for the appetite of those who care about Japanese issues.

Usually, what we call the military is limited to a corner of the army. Why do we disregard the navy? Doesn't Navy Minister Nagano's purge of personnel from the "National Polity Clarification Faction" count as a "military purge"? If it should be included in the military's "military purge" curriculum, why don't we compare it with the army's? This is one of the mysteries of Japanese politics at this stage. Minister of the Army Araki Sadao exhausted all the brains he could think of in the indictment of the "May 15th" incident, using all the words lacking "loyalty to the Emperor and love for the country" in "Words of the Sea" to describe the actions of Lieutenant Kiyoshi Koga. But Navy Minister Uneo Saneomi looked for words in the legal code. During the "February 26th" coup, Miyakezaka became the place where the rebels visited, and the leaders of the rebels, Takashi Muranaka and others, openly handed the "Statement of Intent" and the requested conditions to the "Emperor's" officials. The navy, on the other hand, had no interest in such compromise. Upon hearing the alert, it immediately recalled the training fleet to guard the harbor. On the day of the crisis, it also dispatched marines from Yokosuka to advance towards the capital, causing the Keihin tram to be shut down. After the coup, the so-called "army generals" were busy with the aftermath in the Kaikōsha, and the attitude of General Terauchi, recommended by Minister of the Army Kawashima, became a difficult obstacle to the Hirota cabinet. The navy, however, was very moderate in dealing with it. This shows how different the political attitudes of the army and navy are in the military. The reason for the difference lies in the disparity in tradition, education, etc. This cannot be explained in detail here, but it is enough to point out to our readers that there is a reason why people use the army to represent the military.

No one dares to say that the navy has no factions. Because the terms "Fleet Faction" and "Land Faction," "Militaristic Faction" and "Civilian Faction" are often found in Japanese publications. This kind of factionalism in the navy does not have much impact on the political stage, but the army is not like this. People will use the personnel work of Major General Nagata, the tragic protagonist of the "February 26th" incident, to create the term "Military Purge Faction," etc., in addition to the Araki Faction and the Uga Faction. But from today's perspective, it seems that understanding the lineup of Araki and Uga simply, and understanding the activities of the middle faction—such as Kenkichi Ueda, etc.—makes it easier for us to grasp the position of the military in Japanese political struggles.

Emperor Haile Selassie's Ambition Undiminished: Still Striving for Restoration Movement

(London) Since attending the League of Nations General Assembly at the beginning of last month, the Emperor of Abyssinia has left Swiss territory and is residing here as an exile. Today, he gave an interview to a reporter from the Sunday Chronicle, stating, "I will not give up my ambition to struggle and fight for the independence of my motherland. When I was in Geneva, I submitted a draft resolution to the League of Nations General Assembly, requesting a loan of ten million pounds. Although it failed, the road to borrowing is still not closed. I have formed a committee here to be in charge of debt raising. The results achieved recently are very good, which is enough to invigorate us. Many of my troops are now scattered in the northern and southwestern parts of Abyssinia. From now on, their food and ammunition will be adequately supplied. My duty is to lead the troops and fight to the death with the Italian army. I do not want to die old in a foreign country, ending my life as a fugitive," etc. (2nd day Havas News)

Death of French Airplane Manufacturer: The First Person to Fly Across the English Channel

(Paris) The world's first seaplane aviator, Louis Blériot, passed away here today at the age of sixty-four. Blériot was born in 1872. He studied the design of aircraft structures in his youth, invented a bird-type aircraft, and won a prize of 100,000 francs from the French Academy of Sciences. In 1909, the London Daily Mail offered a prize of 25,000 francs, seeking aviators to make a non-stop flight across the English Channel between sunrise and sunset. Blériot made his own plane and completed the feat on July 24 of that year, becoming the first person to fly across the English Channel. (2nd day National News)

(Paris) The famous French airplane manufacturer, Bleriot, recently passed away here at the age of sixty-four. He flew a self-made small airplane (with an engine of only 35 horsepower) across the Strait of Calais on July 25, 1909. He was the first person to fly across the sea in history. He then devoted himself to the airplane manufacturing business. During the European War, he invented a type of heavy bomber that could rise to an altitude of 6,000 meters, which was a miracle at the time. After the war, he devoted himself to studying the manufacturing method of high-speed airplanes that could ascend to the stratosphere, and also made many contributions. It is not an exaggeration to say that he is a pioneer in the aviation industry. (2nd day Havas News)

(Paris) The famous French aviator Bleriot, the first person to fly across the English Channel, died of illness here today at the age of sixty-four. Bleriot is like the Lindbergh of that time. When he flew across the English Channel in 1909, his great achievement and dangerous feat were the same as Lindbergh's flight across the Atlantic in 1927. Although the two events are eighteen years apart, the names of Bleriot and Lindbergh will be closely linked and shine in the history of aviation. The two men successively achieved great achievements that seemed impossible at the time, and both directly promoted the progress of aviation. It is said that Lindbergh's dedication to aviation was partly motivated by Bleriot's early achievements. In the year Lindbergh became famous, Bleriot's feat had become a daily occurrence, and the progress of the aviation industry was also very rapid. Bleriot was born on July 1, 1872, in Cambrai. His father was a manufacturer, so he came into contact with machinery in his childhood. When he grew up, he studied at a specialized school and obtained an engineering degree. After completing his military service, he served as an artillery officer in Tarbes. In his spare time, he liked to study the structure of automobiles. After several years of experimentation, he invented a car searchlight in 1896. Four years later, the diagram of the famous aircraft built by Ader was displayed at a meeting in Paris. Bleriot was moved by it, so he abandoned the automobile and studied the aviation science that was still in its infancy at that time. Bleriot was determined to make a practical airplane, and he almost forgot to eat and sleep, experimenting more than ten times. The capital he had obtained from his car searchlight was almost completely lost. In 1906, with the help of two friends, he founded the first airplane manufacturing factory in France. On September 17, 1907, Bleriot's dream came true. On that day, he flew his self-made monoplane for a distance of 186 meters. Afterwards, he gradually improved, and other young aviators and manufacturers also came to him. On June 27, 1908, Bleriot flew bravely and won the "Starter Award" of 1,200 francs (equivalent to 10 US dollars). On October 31 of that year, Bleriot made his first long-distance flight, flying from Toury to Artenay, a distance of 60 miles. He stopped once in the middle, and the world was amazed, because at that time, it was almost unbelievable that he could land and take off again with this wonderful machine. The following year, Bleriot conducted a major pre-war aviation experiment, announcing that he would fly across the English Channel on July 25, which shocked the crowd, and many were worried about Bleriot, but Bleriot actually flew from Calais to Dover on that day. The French government sent the destroyer "Escopette" to guide him. At the time, no one expected that Bleriot's speed would exceed that of the destroyer. Bleriot's plane initially flew above the destroyer, but then seemed to be disturbed by the thick smoke emitted by the ship's chimney, so it flew slightly out. As a result, the plane gradually flew forward, and although the destroyer "Escopette" tried to move forward, it could not keep up. Bleriot's plane finally completed the 38-kilometer strait between England and France in 38 minutes. Bleriot's great achievement won him the prize of 1,000 pounds offered by a London newspaper to the first person to fly across the strait. When Bleriot arrived in England, he was warmly welcomed everywhere. When he returned to Paris, his countrymen also held a grand parade to welcome him. The French government also congratulated Bleriot and awarded him the honorary rank of military officer. The plane he flew was on display, and he accepted an invitation from the United States to perform aviation technology. Several years later, Bleriot began to recall the dangers he encountered when flying across the strait, saying that landing was actually unsafe, because he had to inspect the white rocks along the coast of Dover for more than ten minutes before he could identify them. Bleriot had repeatedly encountered dangers when flying for the first time, and his self-made airplane had also crashed many times during test flights. His most proud achievement in his early years was when he was able to stay in the air for eight minutes in a strong wind in July 1908, and in June 1909, he broke the record for staying in the air for a long time three times in a row. The first time he stayed in the air for 18 minutes and 30 seconds, the second time for 36 minutes and 55 seconds, and the third time he reached 50 minutes and 8 seconds. Between 1909 and 1911, Bleriot flew through the capitals of various countries many times, and devoted all his efforts to training young aviators to continue his career. He himself specialized in airplane construction. During the European War, the airplane factory he operated supplied thousands of airplanes to the French and Allied forces. Later, he manufactured a large number of airplanes for French military use. (2nd day Reuters News)

Death of Female Missionary in Beiping

(Beiping) Mrs. Mateer of the American Presbyterian Church died of illness at the age of eighty-six. Mrs. Mateer served the Chinese church for fifty-seven years. She was originally from Massachusetts in the United States and was a relative of the famous American poet Ralph Waldo Emerson. Mrs. Mateer was already in Beiping during the Boxer Rebellion. Afterwards, she took care of her thirty students for many years without changing. Mrs. Mateer was proficient in Chinese and had translated many English books into Chinese. (2nd day Reuters News)
